Page 6

Current Affairs Commentary

Anxiety Amidst Confusion

Yesterday's commentary already pointed out the confusing and bewildering state of the current international situation. It also pointed out that in this confusing and bewildering situation, our country has reached a new and critical juncture. We urged our countrymen to pay close attention to it. After comprehensively analyzing and inferring from the current facts in various aspects, we believe that this confusing situation is increasingly advancing toward a serious future. At the same time, groping under this confusing situation, we feel a great deal of doubt and fear.

Internationally, there is talk of establishing a neutral zone to prevent Japan's continued westward advance and to ease the tension between China and Japan, thereby withdrawing from the situation as soon as possible. However, if the Japanese army does not go beyond Jinzhou and continues westward, the Northeast problem can be left to direct negotiations between China and Japan. This situation can be seen in the Reuters dispatch from Washington on the 30th, stating that the US government believes that the resolution of the Manchurian issue still depends on direct negotiations between China and Japan, as well as Briand's reply to Yoshizawa, stating that extraordinary measures such as sending an investigation team and establishing a neutral zone should not hinder the larger proposals that the Japanese government wants to make to the Chinese government. Moreover, this proposal does not constitute interference from a third party. Since Japan forcibly occupied our Northeast, it believes this is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. It is arrogant and unsatisfied, and wants to extend its control, passing through Shanhaiguan and extending into northern China. However, at the same time, it cannot completely ignore the current international situation. Therefore, its attitude is extremely contradictory, fully exposing the duality of its diplomacy. Sometimes it expresses moderation and withdraws part of its troops. At other times, it suddenly becomes tough, even advocating the establishment of a neutral zone in Hebei, denying the authority of Chinese and Japanese inspectors, and insisting that Chinese troops must withdraw to within the customs, demanding that the Japanese army take so-called anti-bandit military actions in the areas where Chinese troops withdraw. These facts are nothing more than attempts to fatigue international sentiment with a volatile attitude, while also observing the international situation. In addition to occupying the Northeast, it threatens our country to advance its forces westward into northern China, and consolidate the foundation for its second-stage continental policy. This situation is also extremely clear.

We believe that no matter what, today's international mediation and the changes in Japan's attitude are absolutely not in our interest. We try to look back since the League of Nations assembly. Japan has taken the lead at every step, without any scruples. For any claim it makes, the League of Nations always tries to comply. Our country, on the other hand, has failed and retreated at every step. For any appeal we make, the League of Nations turns a deaf ear. The establishment of this neutral zone today may be the confirmation that the Northeast will change hands from now on. The so-called investigation is just a means to step down and deceive the world.

What we are deeply confused and worried about today is how our country should respond to this serious situation. The neutral zone was proposed by us and accepted by the League of Nations. In the near future, it may become a reality. The westward advance of the Japanese army may also be prevented by this buffer zone. But what about the problem east of Jinzhou? Will the establishment of a neutral zone be a means to solve the Northeast problem? Or is it intended to prevent the westward advance of the Japanese army? According to the Havas news agency from Paris on the 30th, it is said that most people believe that the Chinese representatives will eventually agree to the draft resolution, because the troop withdrawal issue was originally the biggest difficulty. It is no longer very important at this point, and what everyone is paying attention to now is the establishment of a neutral zone near the Great Wall. Is that true or not? Is the proposal to withdraw Japanese troops from the Northeast to be abandoned? This is one of the things we are deeply confused and worried about.

Shigemitsu Mamoru arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai on the 30th to discuss the Manchurian neutral zone issue with Foreign Minister Gu. According to Reuters, Tokyo hopes that this discussion can open the way for direct negotiations between China and Japan on the Manchurian issue. At the same time, in Beiping, Japanese representatives have been directly communicating with Zhang Xueliang. Political circles in Tokyo are very optimistic about the future of the overall situation, believing that there will be great progress soon. Does the manifestation of these facts mean that our government is prepared for direct negotiations? Or is it for other diplomatic contacts? If it is prepared for direct negotiations, what is the negotiation strategy? What is the purpose of the negotiations? Will we insist on recovering the lost land? Will we resolutely reject any new conditions or new demands? This is the second thing we are deeply confused and worried about.

We believe that the current confusing situation is enough to make our countrymen imperceptibly fall into an extremely dangerous and tragic situation. It is also enough to make our country fall into a dangerous and tragic situation from which it cannot extricate itself. New bad news and new unfortunate events may suddenly appear under this confusing situation. We are truly filled with anxiety and fear about this.

Domestic Important Telegrams 2

Xinmin County Magistrate

Flees to Jinzhou with Official Seal

(Beiping) After being detained, the Xinmin County Magistrate took the opportunity to escape on the night of the 27th. Carrying the official seal, he detoured through Heishan and Dagushan to meet Rong Zhen in Jinzhou, reporting on the occupation of Xinmin. (Special Dispatch)

Conflicting Japanese Military Intelligence

(Moscow) Since the Japanese army occupied Shenyang, the Japanese army commander Honjo has met with reporters twice. His spokesman, Major Watanabe, provided official information regarding the situation on the various fronts. However, this information should of course be listened to with caution and needs to be further verified. The investigator who went to Qiqihar to visit Commander Domen has now returned to Shenyang. The reason why the official communique from Shenyang needs to be verified is becoming increasingly clear. Arranging and comparing the news released by the Japanese officials in Shenyang and Heihe will be very interesting reading.

From Commander Honjo's Side

On November 22nd, he stated that 31 Japanese soldiers were killed and 104 were wounded.

The number of Chinese soldiers killed, based on the bodies found on the battlefield, is about 600. In the Angxi battle, there were 3,500 Japanese soldiers.

On the morning of November 18th, when the first line of Chinese defense had not been broken, the fighting was very fierce.

On the evening of November 18th, the Qiqihar station on the Chinese Eastern Railway was occupied. Honjo repeatedly said that Ma Zhanshan must have received Russian assistance. At least five people heard the investigator say this.

On the 24th, he stated that he had not heard of the withdrawal of troops from Qiqihar. A Japanese soldier named Yamada was detained and tortured by Chinese people, and then secretly released by a Korean prison officer.

From Commander Domen's Side

On November 20th, he stated that 51 Japanese soldiers were killed and over 200 were wounded.

Approximately 200 Chinese soldiers were killed.

In the Angxi battle, there were 5,000 Japanese soldiers.

The first line of Chinese defense was easily broken. The fierce fighting was north of the Chinese Eastern Railway, on the night of November 18th.

Japanese soldiers did not get close to the Qiqihar station. Japanese soldiers crossed the Chinese Eastern Railway line 4 kilometers east of the station.

The Russians did not assist Ma.

On the 20th, he stated that he was ordered to withdraw a regiment of infantry and an artillery unit to Taonan or Changchun when the railway was repaired.

Yamada was released by the Chinese and returned safely, with no mention of torture. (Reuters, 30th)

Source of Ma's Arms and Ammunition

Japanese Smuggling Agency Uncovered

The Theory of Soviet Assistance Appears Unfounded

(Moscow) The Russian official TASS news agency received a telegram from Beiping, mentioning that the Japanese were privately transporting military supplies to Ma Zhanshan. According to recent news, many people have been arrested in Dalian and Shenyang, mostly Japanese employees of government or semi-government agencies. Among them are an American and several Poles and Lithuanians. This case is currently under investigation, but the investigation is being conducted in great secrecy because it has been discovered that important Japanese officials in Manchuria and personnel from other countries are backing this smuggling agency. It is rumored that three train cars of military supplies were transported from Dalian to Qiqihar, but were detained by the Chinese police in Shenyang. (Reuters, 30th)

(Shenyang) The mystery of the source of Ma Zhanshan's military supplies now seems to be coming to light. For weeks, people have been accusing the Soviet Union of supplying military supplies to the Chinese army in northern Manchuria to resist the Japanese. The Russian Foreign Minister has formally and firmly denied this. The Japanese government has also stated that officials have never claimed that Russia secretly aided the Chinese army. However, the commander of the Japanese army in Manchuria, Honjo, has repeatedly told reporters that Ma Zhanshan must have received Soviet assistance. Today, it has been learned that the people who are supplying military supplies to the Chinese army in northern Manchuria to resist the Japanese are the Japanese themselves. The Japanese newspapers published in Dalian, Dalian News and Manchuria Daily, both carried the following news. It is said that the Japanese police in Shenyang detained a box of military supplies at the Shenyang station. After a preliminary investigation, it was discovered that the company that transported the box of military supplies was a certain transportation company in Dalian, and other transportation companies, Dalian customs officials, and Chinese and foreign employees of the South Manchuria Railway Bureau were all involved in this case. These military supplies were being transported to Harbin for use by the Chinese army and bandits. This is what the Japanese newspapers reported. It has been discovered that the so-called most involved company is a famous Japanese company, whose head office is located in Dalian. Two days later, the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun carried a telegram from a special investigator in Dalian, which read: "The Dalian police have discovered that someone is privately smuggling military supplies to northern Manchuria with the assistance of customs officials and employees of a certain large company. The businesses engaged in this private smuggling of military supplies include Japanese, Chinese, and foreigners. Therefore, the police stations in Manchuria have launched a joint operation to search for the criminals. On November 18th, the Dalian police arrested two customs officials, several employees of a certain company, and several others, who are all under investigation." After this case was announced by the Japanese newspapers, there has been no further news to date. It is suspected that news about this case has been withheld by military censors. (Reuters, 30th)

British House of Commons

Discusses the Situation in Eastern Provinces

London British Foreign Secretary Simon made a lengthy speech in the House of Commons today, discussing the situation in Manchuria and how to protect the interests of British and Japanese creditors of the Beining Railway. Simon stated that the League of Nations Council is continuing its efforts, hoping to find a solution to the Manchurian problem. The joint efforts of the Council are expected to be successful. The revenue of the Beining Railway has decreased significantly due to recent events. Negotiations on this matter are currently underway. Changes in the administrative structure of Shenyang have made it difficult to transfer funds owed to British interests, and payments for goods purchased from British companies by the Railway Bureau have also been delayed. According to reports from the British side, there have been no battles between China and Japan in the past ten days. Newspapers are now carrying news that the Japanese army is currently retreating into the South Manchuria Railway area, but officials have not yet received reports confirming this statement. Labor Party member Wedgwood Benn stated that the UK's top priority is to avoid the constraints of sanctions and other similar forms of war. The Foreign Secretary replied that the British government is very eager to avoid the use of sanctions in any dispute handled by the League of Nations and, therefore, is focused on seeking a peaceful solution with other members of the Council. This principle is the foundation of the League of Nations charter, and the mechanisms in the charter for taking collective action are also based on this. Liberal Party member Mayson stated, "Japan is disregarding Articles 12, 13, and 15 of the charter. What steps will the British government take on this matter? Please announce them." The Foreign Secretary replied, only stating that the League of Nations is currently handling this issue. Under the current circumstances, it is best to let the Council deliberate on the matter. He also stated that the legitimate demands of British creditors of the Chinese government, arising from overdue payments of principal and interest on railway loans, will be raised when the time is right. (Reuters, 30th)

US and Japan Reconcile

Stimson Unwilling to Talk Much About the Situation in the Eastern Provinces

(Washington) US Secretary of State Stimson, in light of the fact that the previous dissemination of mild criticism had angered the Japanese, was unwilling to discuss the Manchurian situation at all when he met with reporters today. He merely stated that he believed he had said enough about the tense situation between China and Japan and that there was no need to say more. On the Japanese side, after Stimson denied criticizing the Japanese government's remarks, it declared to the US government that the previous declaration criticizing Stimson was issued by the Japanese Foreign Ministry but had not been approved by Foreign Minister Kijūrō Shidehara. The Japanese ambassador to the United States, Debuchi, specially went to the State Department today to solemnly declare this intention to Stimson. Therefore, now that Stimson's remarks have been denied and the Japanese side's declaration has been withdrawn, the two countries have reconciled. (National News Agency, 30th)

Ma Zhanshan

Reply to the Fourth Plenary Session of the Guangdong Party Congress

Hailun Ma Zhanshan's reply to the Fourth National Congress of the Kuomintang in Guangzhou reads, "I have just received your telegram, and I am deeply grateful for your compliments. This time, the violent Japanese are relying on their strength to be fierce and brutal, trampling on our country, disregarding the great powers, and disregarding peace treaties and international integrity. They are truly the common enemy of mankind and an obstacle to peace. However, things must rot before worms grow, and a country must defeat itself before others defeat it. Since those ambitious people have been eyeing Jiang province, envoys from friendly countries have been inspecting us one after another. Those who earnestly express goodwill towards us all feel that it is a pity that our national spirit has failed to unite and that it is difficult to achieve consistency in the face of events. The Congress is made up of the advanced members of the Party and the country, and I hope that you can address this weakness. If the Northeast is lost, the country will no longer be a country. I earnestly request that you actively find ways to eliminate party strife, awaken the people, and unite against foreign aggression, striving for the survival of the nation and the status of the country. The Party and the country may then have hope. Zhanshan is a mere military man who has pledged himself to the country. I do not know anything other than defense. However, because I am at the forefront and most deeply stimulated, I have received compliments from afar and offer my humble suggestions, hoping that you will consider them." (Special Dispatch, 30th)

The Neutral Zone

Must Have Troops Stationed by the Great Powers

Remarks from a Certain Important Diplomat

(Nanjing) A certain diplomat said, "The neutral zone issue, as reported by Paris, is slightly different from the content of the government's instructions to Ambassador Shi. Originally, this proposal was proposed by the Chinese side in response to the urgent situation at the time. It is necessary for the countries to send troops to station in the neutral zone to impartially judge the right and wrong between China and Japan, and then it can be called a neutral term. In this way, the Chinese army can also reluctantly retreat. Now that the countries have refused to send troops to participate, the so-called neutral zone term is not applicable. Therefore, the government believes that if the countries do not send troops, the neutral term does not need to exist, and there is no talk of withdrawing troops from Jinzhou. At present, only the work of the observation group is being done. Negotiations on this observation group have been ongoing with the British, American, and French ambassadors in recent days. The three ambassadors believe that Japan needs to restrict the scope of observation. Therefore, the three governments have not yet given a definite answer to this proposal." (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Acceptance of Mediation Method

The 24 members elected by the Nanjing side may be recognized by a two-thirds vote of the Fourth Central Committee at its first congress. 3. Party members who were expelled from the Party for political reasons in the past, except for communists, will generally have their Party membership restored. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Establishment of the Highest

Pacification Organs in Jiangxi, Henan, and Hubei

(Nanjing) After the completion of the headquarters, the various field headquarters will also be abolished accordingly. However, the three provinces of Jiangxi, Henan, and Hubei have special circumstances in fact, and there cannot be a lack of command and control organs. Therefore, provisional highest pacification organs will be established in each province to unify and continue the suppression of bandits. The districts under the jurisdiction of the specially appointed pacification directors are as follows: 1. The Jiangxi Pacification District includes all of Jiangxi Province, as well as the areas east of the Yuehan Railway in Hunan Province, and the Li belongs of Anhui Province, the Qu belongs of Zhejiang Province, and the Tingzhang belongs of Fujian Province. Matters concerning the pacification of the southeast Yang Dakaitong area of Hubei Province must be coordinated with the Pacification Director stationed in Hubei. 2. The Henan Pacification District includes all of Henan Province, as well as Hedong in Shanxi Province, Tongguan in Shaanxi Province, the western part of Anhui Province, and the southern part of Hebei Province. In the pacification area of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui, matters concerning the pacification of the northeastern part of Hubei Province must be coordinated with the Pacification Director stationed in Hubei. 3. The Hubei Pacification District includes all of Hubei Province, as well as southern Shaanxi, eastern Sichuan, northern Hunan, and the pacification matters of each southeastern region. It must be coordinated with the Sichuan Supervising Officer Liu, the Shaanxi Chairman Yang, and the Pacification Director. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

(Hankou) The reorganization of the Field Headquarters into the Pacification Office has been postponed due to the fact that the organizational law has not been promulgated. Generally, it will be implemented after He returns to Hankou after asking for instructions in Nanjing. (Special Dispatch, 1st)

Matters Handed Over by Headquarters

The Fourth Route Fortress Command Will Not Be Abolished

(Nanjing) After the completion of the Army, Navy, and Air Force Headquarters, various military and political matters have been assigned to the three departments of Staff, Military Affairs, and Training and Supervision to take over. Central Principal

Proclamation to Students

(Nanjing) Zhu Jiahua, President of Central University, today issued a proclamation to students, saying: There is more than one way to save the country. The government is responsible for strategic planning and decisive victories. Students should focus on their studies to prepare themselves with knowledge and achieve the best results in saving the country through academic pursuits. If they abandon their studies, run around and shout slogans, regardless of the actual benefits, it would mean that thousands of promising young people each waste an hour of study, totaling over two thousand hours of knowledge that should have been acquired. This also means losing some basic strength in the work of saving the country. Moreover, our university is the highest institution of learning in the capital, and the words and actions of its students are observed by students across the country, with far-reaching influence related to the future of the nation. It is crucial to carefully consider these matters. As the president, my concern for the country is no less than anyone else's. However, while I commend the students' aspirations to save the country, their methods are not necessarily correct. Therefore, I issue this sincere proclamation, hoping that all students will work hard, strive for progress, and devote themselves to research. Adopt the spirit of perseverance, to achieve the best results in averting danger and stabilizing the situation. Do not waste time and abandon studies, hindering the fundamental strength needed to save the country. (One-day special dispatch)

Ban on Export of Silver

Ministry of Finance Plans Measures

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, considering the significant impact on the economy and finance due to the large-scale export of silver, has formulated measures to ban it. 1. The Bankers' Association will organize a registered silver investigation team. From now on, all banks and merchants must report their silver inflows, outflows, uses, and storage amounts to the Bankers' Association for verification on a daily basis. 2. Customs will inspect the transportation of silver to and from various ports. Merchants must obtain passports and certificates from the local chairman, proving the destination, purpose, and use of the silver, ensuring there is no smuggling. Otherwise, the entire amount will be confiscated. 3. In addition to the originally defined maritime area, customs will exercise its anti-smuggling authority to strictly inspect all Chinese and foreign merchant ships. Anti-smuggling teams will be added and patrol thoroughly. These measures have been ordered to be followed by all customs offices and the Shanghai Bankers' Association. (One-day special dispatch)

Zhang Xianglin was appointed as Director of the Intelligence Department. Jin Wensi, Zhao Quanzhu, and Xing Yuan were appointed as Counselors. Before Changci Wang Jiazhen returns to the country, Jin Wensi will temporarily serve as Changci. Yang Yongqing, Yang Nianzu, and Zhang Shanbao were appointed as Secretaries. Xu Ding was appointed as Head of the Document Section, Li Hongshi as Head of the Telegraph Section, Chen Weiping as Head of the Accounting Section, Ge Zukang as Head of the General Affairs Section, Huang Yuding as Head of the Cashier Section, and Xie Jialiu as Head of the Seal Section. Yan Youqiao was appointed as the Director of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' Shanghai Office. Fan Guang, Zhao Cisheng, and Ying Shangde were appointed as advisors to the Treaty Committee. Diao Minqian, Jin Zhiji, and Ji Jing were appointed as members of the Treaty Committee. Xu Mo remains the Director of the European and American Affairs Department. Foreign Telegrams

British-Indian Round Table Conference

Gandhi Strives for Independence

British Government Promises India Provisional Autonomy

Declaration to be Released Soon

London, 30th, National Telegram: At last night's meeting of the Second Indian Round Table Conference, Gandhi made a surprising speech. He demanded absolute independence for India, otherwise, he may have to continue his non-violent resistance movement. Sunday, as usual, was Gandhi's day of silence, so Gandhi did not speak until after midnight. Gandhi coughed severely while speaking, stopping frequently. Gandhi said, "What I want is complete independence for India. I want to exhaust my brain and blood to find a bright way to solve the problem, so that the millions of people in India will not suffer the pain of non-violent resistance again. But if even this is unavoidable, I will face it with a smile. Can you allow me to exchange this temporary truce for permanent peace?" Gandhi admitted that if Britain could give India true independence, he would be willing to make the necessary concessions. As for the minority issues among the ethnic groups in India, he said that there are ways to solve them. He did not express despair.

Reuters, London, 1st: British Prime Minister MacDonald will submit a statement of the British government's policy on India to the Indian Round Table Conference today. The representatives attach great importance to this matter. Yesterday, they discussed it at St. James's Palace for more than fourteen hours, from 10:30 in the morning until 2:15 this morning, with only a short break in between. Chairman MacDonald rushed to a special cabinet meeting after 9 o'clock, which was convened specifically to consider MacDonald's statement. This morning, the newspapers predicted that the Prime Minister would announce the British government's policy, which is to allow India temporary autonomy and central responsibility, and suggest sending a parliamentary committee to India to work with the Indian committee compiling the Indian central constitution. It is said that Lord Sankey will be the chairman of the committee.

Hungary

Coup Plot Discovered

Related to Restoration Plan

Budapest, 30th, Havas Telegram: Recent reports in the newspapers stated that a conspiracy case was discovered in Budapest, Hungary. This matter has been officially announced to prove it is true. The conspiracy planned to disrupt order. The rebels seemed to have infiltrated the barracks and police stations with forged orders, intending to organize a dictatorial regime similar to the Soviet Union. The date of their uprising was delayed to November 21 for unknown reasons. However, as the authorities had already noticed, it was decided that the uprising must be launched by the 28th at the latest. The government took necessary measures and arrested the masterminds and other important party members on the 27th. The action was very swift, showing that the government still has the ability to maintain order. From the rebels' confessions, it was learned that this conspiracy did not receive the support of the people, and its members did not belong to any political party in the parliament. It was also discovered that the rebels had an executive committee, with 150 to 200 people assisting them, but they were completely unaware of the masterminds' plans.

Budapest, 30th, National Telegram: Last night, the authorities arrested many political prisoners, reportedly related to the discovered restoration conspiracy. Rumors said that the party members planned to make Archduke Otto king, and Archduke Otto was almost arrested as well. However, the authorities are still tight-lipped about this matter.

Italy and Hungary Conclude Secret Air Force Pact

Paris, 1st, National Telegram: This morning, the People's Daily reported that as a result of the recent visit of Italian Air Minister Balbo to Hungary, a secret air force pact between Italy and Hungary has been concluded. Italy will bear the majority of the construction costs.

Britain and France to Hold Economic Talks

Paris, 1st, Reuters Telegram: Today, according to official sources, Britain and France will soon hold talks to reach an agreement on various economic issues. This announcement is rather vague, but the purpose of Finance Minister Flandin's visit to Britain can be guessed. When Flandin left Paris, he claimed to be going to Britain for hunting, but it is now known that Flandin stayed in London for several days and had very important political discussions. Flandin is still silent and neither denies nor admits that his trip had any political effect. This morning, a guest said that he did not discuss tax rates, but admitted that he had briefly discussed matters such as the stabilization of the pound, war debts, and reparations with British politicians. He also said that tax rate issues are purely within the purview of the Minister of Commerce, and he should not overstep his bounds. He was very happy to get to know British Chancellor of the Exchequer Chamberlain, because France will soon have some important issues to resolve with him. It is evident that British and French views currently differ on war debts, debts, tax rates, and reparations. The public believes this is unfortunate and that it is in the best interests of both countries to strive for a better understanding.

Disputes Over Japan's Tax Increase Plan

Tokyo, 1st, Electric Communication Telegram: Finance Minister Inoue submitted the tax increase plan yesterday afternoon, seeking the understanding of the party's top executives. Because the summer expenditure for Showa 7 is estimated at 1,479 million yen, while the revenue is only 1,307 million yen, there is a shortfall of 172 million yen. The proposed method of compensation is to increase taxes and raise debts, namely: (1) Business bonds of 67 million yen; (2) Tax increase of 40 million yen; Deficit-covering bonds of 65 million yen. In this way, the balance of income and expenditure can be expected.

Another telegram: Regarding the revenue compensation plan, party leaders all advocated revising tariffs and suspending tax increases. However, Inoue believed that the income from revising tariffs was uncertain and could not be regarded as a permanent source of revenue, expressing opposition. Only minor adjustments can be made to the item details of the building category.

Another telegram: Within the party, regarding the Finance Minister's tax increase plan, it is advocated to raise tariffs on wheat and other items to fill the deficit and suspend the tax increase plan. It is felt that the tax increase plan includes a tariff revision plan to reduce the burden on the people. If it is still insufficient, then it can be remedied by the debt reduction fund. The opinions of both sides are vastly different. Prime Minister Wakatsuki invited advisor Tomida Raimu yesterday morning to explain the unavoidable circumstances of raising debt and increasing taxes in the budget preparation, and said that he regretted the internal strife caused by raising debt. The government will refer to the opinions of the party and make partial revisions, but it still hopes to maintain the original plan of the Ministry of Finance.

Bulgarian Prime Minister to Turkey to Conclude New Treaty

It is expected that during his stay in Istanbul, he will negotiate a border protection treaty with the Turkish government. It is also expected that a commercial treaty will be negotiated. Zhang Zhanshan obeyed the orders carefully, only striving to do his best and fulfill his duty to defend the territory. For the sake of the country and the people, Zhang Zhanshan had no choice but to resort to legitimate defense. Since then, everything from defense and combat to supply and support has been planned and maintained by the Commander-in-Chief and Deputy Commander-in-Chief. Zhang Zhanshan only obeyed and followed. The Commander-in-Chief and Deputy Commander-in-Chief knew the disparity in strength between the enemy and us, and all available support troops were mobilized one by one, without waiting for Zhang Zhanshan's request. I am grateful for the encouragement from wise men at home and abroad. Reflecting on myself, I am deeply ashamed. However, without the care and guidance of the Commander-in-Chief and Deputy Commander-in-Chief and the cooperation and support of the allied forces, even with the authority to confront the strong enemy for several days, I am afraid I would not have been able to do so. In the future, my actions will still be subject to the orders of the Commander-in-Chief and Deputy Commander-in-Chief. I am honored to receive attention. I dare to state my sincerity and hope that you will understand my sincerity and issue instructions from time to time. Ma Zhanshan stamped.

Important News

Japanese Troops

The Situation in Jilin and Changchun Under the Iron Heel

Japanese Aggressively Expand Political and Economic Influence

Beijing Correspondence: Since the Japanese army seized our Liaoning and Jilin provinces, their measures have been extremely brutal. A gentleman from Changchun recently arrived in Beijing and described the situation in Jilin and Changchun. He said that Jilin is now blockaded by the Japanese. Not only can news from within the province not be transmitted outwards, but information from the outside world cannot enter. A brief account of his words is as follows:

Blockading News: The only newspaper published in Changchun is the Datong Daily. It usually takes an anti-Japanese stance, and its attacks were especially fierce when the "Wan Incident" occurred. The Japanese hated it to the bone. This time, when the Japanese army entered the city, the head of the military police summoned the newspaper's manager, threatened him, and the manager was able to adapt and reverse his previous attitude, and was fortunately preserved. It is still published as usual, but manuscripts must be inspected before they can be printed. Every day, there are articles praising and extolling the Japanese, which is the same as the "Three Eastern Provinces People's Daily" in Shenyang, and are driven and exploited by the Japanese. In Jilin City, there is the "Jichang Daily," which is subsidized by Xi Qia and directed by the Japanese. Reporters stationed in Changchun from Beiping, Tianjin, and Shanghai were initially able to communicate occasionally, reporting the brutal acts of the Japanese army. However, later, due to the strict censorship of the post office, not only were the letters confiscated, but the military police even searched according to the addresses and gave serious warnings to the correspondents. In early November, Bai Xiaofeng, a correspondent for the Tianjin Yishi Daily, was arrested and taken away by the military police. After being severely beaten, he has not yet been released. All newspapers from Beiping, Tianjin, and Shanghai are detained by the Japanese army as soon as they arrive in Changchun. Dozens of newspaper deliverers have lost their jobs, and the import of news has also been cut off. Thus, the Japanese successfully blockaded the news.

Strengthening Military Preparations: Since the Nanling barracks were occupied by the Japanese army, they have invested 500,000 yuan to renovate them. The work was completed in early November. A regiment each of infantry and artillery are stationed there, and the remaining houses are rented to Japanese merchants to open restaurants. Police stations and Japanese military police substations have also been established, and the nearby streets have been renamed Nanling-cho and Itchome, Nichome, etc. All facilities are no different from the occupied land of the South Manchuria Railway. Moreover, in the area of ​​the Lijia Oil Mill, ten li northwest of Changchun City, 3,800 mu of civilian land were forcibly purchased to build an airfield and aircraft hangar, all of which have been completed. Twelve airplanes have been placed there, and the stored oil is sufficient for more than one hundred airplanes for one year. From the beginning of October, the Japanese barracks within the occupied land of the South Manchuria Railway have been constantly transporting whole train cars of military supplies from Lushun and Dalian. It is said that the ordnance stored in its underground warehouses is sufficient for 50,000 people to fight for five years, which is used to guard against the southward invasion of Russian forces in the North Manchuria region.

Merging the Two Railways: The Jidun and Jichang Railways, through Jin Bitong (son of Prince Su of the former Qing Dynasty) and the Japanese Nakagawa Zensho (former representative of the South Manchuria Railway dispatched to the Jichang Railway), have signed a secret agreement to implement the merger. Starting from December 1st, direct through-trains will be opened, and the line will be renamed Changdun Railway. The Changchun Railway Station in front of the Changchun South Manchuria Railway Station was formerly known as Changchun Station, and the Jichang Railway Station was formerly known as Toutaogou Station. Now the Jichang Railway Station is named Changchun Station, and the South Manchuria Railway Station is renamed East Station. It is said that the secret agreement for the merger was signed on October 28th. In addition to the Japanese representative, the Chinese parties involved were Xi Qia and Jin Bitong. In order to implement the merger, the Japanese side specially sent Xi Qia and Jin Bitong 1 million Japanese yen each as a reward.

Seizing the Electricity Industry: The Changchun Electric Light Plant is a commercial enterprise run by the Jilin Provincial Bank. At the end of September, the Japanese army sent troops to guard it, and the South Manchuria Electric Company sent Qiao to serve as a consultant to the plant. Later, the Japanese army headquarters summoned Gao Wuzi, the director of the plant, and ordered him to sign a 50-year lease contract. Wu refused and argued with Duomen, with strong reasoning and a vow not to sign. Seeing that the plan was not working, Duomen went to Jilin and ordered Xi Qia to remove Wu. Xi Qia obeyed and dismissed Wu on November 24th, and appointed Wu Renpu to take over. The electricity lease contract is expected to be signed soon. The Changchun electricity industry will be lost to others from now on. It is said that the content of the lease is that the Changchun Chinese Electric Light Plant leases electricity from the South Manchuria Electric Company to provide sufficient power. For each kilowatt of electricity used, a fee of 3 Japanese sen per day is paid, for a period of 50 years. The plant must also permanently hire Japanese people as supervisors to manage all financial matters. The full text has ten articles, and this is its general outline.

Commercial Decline: Changchun's commercial district used to be a lively place, but in the past two months, the roads have been quiet and deserted, and shops have been closed. Red paper notices for vacant rentals and store transfer are everywhere. According to the Chamber of Commerce, over 200 businesses have closed down in the past two months. The largest department store in the city, the Xiehe Shopping Mall, used to sell 2,000 yuan per day, but now it sells less than 200 yuan. Other foreign goods stores that used to sell 400-500 yuan per day now sell less than 20-30 yuan. The desolate scene is evident. Moreover, the Japanese army is negotiating to place two Japanese advisors in the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. It is foreseeable that Changchun's commerce will be completely controlled by the Japanese.

Japanese Military Demonstrations: After the Japanese army occupied Changchun on September 19th, they sent troops to guard all institutions such as the electric light plant, telegraph and telephone bureau, public security bureau, and municipal government office, and they have not yet withdrawn. Their armed battalions patrol the streets every day. Recently, because the Second Division was sent to the Tao'ang Railway line to conquer Heilongjiang Province, Changchun's defenses were weak. Therefore, the Japanese Commercial School students organized a volunteer army to help maintain order. Most of the students in the school are young children, mostly only ten years old or so, and they are also carrying guns and ammunition, demonstrating in the city every day. The South Manchuria Railway garrison also patrols from time to time. The Haicheng artillery team sometimes drags more than a dozen large cannons and armored vehicles, slowly moving on the streets. Therefore, Japanese troops pass by every street every half hour. The Japanese army also took three gold watches from

Page 10

Shenchang Clock Shop, paying only 3 Japanese yen. The Japanese troops guarding the electric light plant took the wristwatches of the plant workers. Other acts, such as not paying for rides, not paying for goods purchased, and beating Chinese people for no reason, are too numerous to mention. Pedestrians at midnight are often considered spies and shot to death. After nine o'clock, there is no one on the streets except for guards and patrol police. In addition, Japanese police investigate household registrations, arrest people at will, search schools, and Korean and Japanese ronin commit robberies, and traitors take advantage of the situation. Such actions occur every day, which is truly painful. (November 30th)

Pu Wei's Photo Upon Arrival in Shenyang

× Marks Pu Wei ○ Marks Pu Wei's Japanese Advisor Major Ataku

Prelude to the Japanese Cabinet's Shakeup

Coalition Cabinet Still in the Works

Tokyo Correspondence: The curtain on the Japanese political situation has slowly begun to rise. Although Agriculture Minister Machida, Prime Minister Sakurai, Justice Minister Watanabe, Communications Minister Koizumi, Finance Minister Inoue, and others have been focusing on the current situation, doing their best to encourage Prime Minister Wakatsuki to take a hard line, the future remains uncertain until Home Minister Adachi returns to Tokyo. On the 21st, Adachi returned to Tokyo from the army exercise grounds, covered in dust from his journey. As soon as he took off his luggage, he issued a statement in the form of a speech. The main points were: "The current situation has reached a critical point. Therefore, if the nation's beliefs and determination recognize the possibility of creating a 'national cabinet based on the cooperation of political parties,' then it can be done at any time. There is no need for any hesitation here." While issuing the statement, Home Minister Adachi decided to avoid all unpublicized behind-the-scenes maneuvering, intending to openly negotiate directly with the Seiyukai party.

Like a bolt from the blue, the entire party government was shaken. The result of the meeting between the two giants Wakatsuki and Adachi on the 22nd revealed even greater flaws. Wakatsuki said, "I agree with the ideal of a cooperative cabinet. It would be great if it could be realized, but it is currently impossible. Therefore, it is better not to talk about it." Adachi said, "Realization is difficult, but we cannot conclude that it is impossible. If it is truly impossible in the future, then we will do what we can with the current situation at that time." These two opinions are diametrically opposed, adding a heavy layer of grey to the fate of the current cabinet. At the same time, a direct conflict apparently occurred between Prime Minister Wakatsuki and Home Minister Adachi, leading to the ______ of the cabinet, ______ confrontation.

The Gateway of the Shenyang Puppet Government Construction Research Association

If Prime Minister Wakatsuki strongly advocates maintaining the status quo, Home Minister Adachi is extremely supportive of a coalition cabinet. In this context, the words and actions of the opposition Seiyukai party are worthy of attention. Recently, Seiyukai Secretary-General Kuhara visited Kinmochi Saionji, stating the Seiyukai's position, roughly saying, "A coalition cabinet violates the normal path of constitutionalism. At the same time, it is completely incompatible with our party's principles. Two political parties from the ruling and opposition parties with completely different policies suddenly join hands, which is political suicide. For example, on issues such as the gold embargo and diplomacy, there is absolutely no possibility of cooperation between the Seiyukai and the current cabinet. At this time, the Seiyukai has decided to reject all temptations and strive to form a new, independent cabinet." This statement, whether viewed from the facts or from the theory, seems to have considerable grounds for existence. At the same time, it clearly expresses the Seiyukai's non-cooperation policy, adding another layer of shadow to the formation of a coalition cabinet. Before today's major and difficult situation, there is indeed a need to create a national united coalition cabinet. In today's world, any national with a supra-partisan patriotic heart would not oppose the appearance of a coalition cabinet. In other words, anyone who opposes a coalition cabinet can be said to be unpatriotic." This was the statement issued by Home Minister Adachi during a meeting with the Minseito party's executives on the 23rd. Under the current circumstances, the Seiyukai has already distanced itself, opposing a coalition cabinet, while Wakatsuki is resolutely advocating maintaining the status quo. Adachi, in the face of these two major difficulties, cannot but make this more explicit statement. At the same time, in order to satisfy the demands of the "Adachi faction," he cannot but make this more explicit statement. This statement can not only consolidate Adachi's own political position, but also give the coalition cabinet movement some sensation. The Minseito party originally held a very large majority in the parliament. This time, Adachi's decisive emergence is tantamount to turning against the party. However, as far as Home Minister Adachi himself is concerned, it is recently impossible to join hands with Wakatsuki again, abandon the proposition of a coalition cabinet, and put his own politics in a suicidal situation. Adachi cannot invite Wakatsuki to compromise, nor can he cooperate with the Seiyukai, and he is unwilling to abandon his previous proposals. In the end, whether he intends to win over a part of the Minseito and establish a new party remains to be seen.

In short, if a coalition cabinet can be formed, the "Wakatsuki Cabinet" will inevitably collapse. Conversely, if a coalition cabinet cannot be formed, then Adachi, for the sake of his own political position, can only resort to resignation. However, Home Minister Adachi's resignation may still induce the collapse of the current cabinet.

Caught between a wolf in front and a tiger behind, in a dilemma, the life of the Wakatsuki Cabinet may be buried in this prelude to a coalition cabinet. (Published by Shou on November 24th)

Xuzhou Students Petition in Beijing

Urging the Government to Recover Lost Territories

Presenting Four Matters to Chairman Chiang

Xuzhou Correspondence: The Xuzhou Student Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association petition group has departed for Beijing to petition Chiang. The group departed in batches on the 29th and 30th. The group is organized by seven secondary schools into eight teams. The teams are: 1st Xuzhou Middle School, 2nd Xuzhou Middle School, Xuzhou Girls' Middle School, Zhengxin, Peixin, Private Xuzhou, Tongshan Normal, and Art Academy. Each team elected one person to be the presidium. The candidates were Xu Tongyi, Peng Ying, Han Ruchun, Wang Yiyin, Wang Jizhou, Wu Xiaosa, Sun Chuanwen, and Wu Binlian. Xu Xienong, a teacher from the 1st Xuzhou Middle School, was invited to be the commander-in-chief, and Gu Zuhua from the 2nd Xuzhou Middle School and Zhu Dezhang from Private Xuzhou were invited to be the deputy commanders. Each team also elected one commander and one deputy commander to lead. Before departure, the headquarters stipulated the following creeds: (1) Obey orders, (2) Endure hardship, (3) Help each other, (4) Maintain neat ranks. The first batch assembled at the East Railway Station on the afternoon of the 29th and boarded the train south. At that time, the Garrison Headquarters had received a telegram from Beijing ordering them to persuade the students to stop going to Beijing. The department instructed the county government to handle the matter. The county party headquarters also received a central telegram advising them to stop the students. However, the students were determined to go and the persuasion was ineffective. The Jinpu Station Master immediately telegraphed the Pukou Management Committee for instructions. The reply was to handle the matter carefully. Before long, the special train of Commander Wang sent to greet him was also prepared to go south. The railway then attached several passenger cars. The first batch of students then boarded the train and went south. The second batch boarded the Pingpu train that night. The third batch departed on another train on the 30th. In two days, a total of three batches departed, with a total of more than 1,000 people. The students were all wearing uniforms and did not bring bedding. Each person had several pounds of dry pancakes for several days of food. Their spirit of hardship and perseverance is admirable. It is planned that all three batches of students will gather at the Central University and present four petitions to Chairman Chiang in person. The petition reads: "Respectfully presented, since the brutal Japanese occupied our Northeast, their fierce flames have become more and more intense, and more and more land has been lost. The League of Nations has lost its credibility, and Ma Jun is in isolated danger. At this critical moment, it is difficult to sweep away the evil atmosphere unless we personally carry out heavenly punishment. Therefore, the people of the country hope that our public sentiment is more urgent than a shooting star. When Duke Guo Linggong went to the east, the thieves were all terrified. When Emperor Zhenzong of Song personally led the expedition to Chanyuan, the morale of the soldiers increased. Now is the time. Recently, we heard that the Fourth Plenary Session has passed the proposal to defend national rights and protect national territory, and that Your Excellency also has the determination to recover the lost territories in the shortest possible time. A cloud of hope in a great drought, a timely rain from the royal army, not only the people of the East have this desire, but also the people of the whole country are grateful and tearful. We continue to write about saving the country, with two thoughts intertwined. We vow not to be slaves of a fallen country. How fortunate to hear the training of the oath, so we are sincerely worried, bleeding our hearts, kowtowing nine times before the army, and again speaking to the commander. First, we ask our Chairman to go north to defend the country. The sooner we kill the enemy, the sooner we save the country. Second, we ask our Chairman to strictly order Zhang Xueliang, who lost the territory, to quickly gather the remnants and make meritorious service to atone for his sins. Encourage him to learn from Feng Xiaoyang's Mianchi's struggle, and not just be like Chen Shubao who has no heart and soul. Third, we ask our Chairman to issue firearms to the schools in Xuzhou, so that the volunteer army can be established as soon as possible. Since Xuzhou has had many strong men since ancient times, if they can be trained, they will naturally become a powerful army. Fourth, we ask our Chairman to clearly order the governments of various places to do their best to protect the patriotic movement, because force is the vanguard of defeating the enemy, and refusing goods is the shield of revenge. We are not talented, and present four matters. We beg for your instruction. We hate that we cannot follow you closely and contribute to the Yanran's achievements. We are fortunate to see the vehicles and horses go far, and we will see the Xianyun's support. Nan Zhong has prestige, and the north wind is strong. Take care of your journey ahead, and listen to the triumphal song. With the most sincere enthusiasm, we gather a group of more than 2,000 people to visit the capital and show our hearts and offer advice to the country. We respectfully ask for your decision. The Xuzhou Student Petition Group of 2,000 people kowtow together." In addition, they also sent out a circular telegram, a declaration, and a letter to fellow countrymen. When each batch of students boarded the train, they shouted slogans, and people from all walks of life went to the station to see them off, which was extremely enthusiastic and impassioned. (November 30th)

Executive Yuan

47th National Affairs Meeting

Passed Measures to Exempt Native Cloth from Business Tax

Resolved to Participate in the American People's Art Exhibition

The Executive Yuan held its 47th National Affairs Meeting on the morning of the 1st. Song Ziwen, Liu Ruiheng, Li Shuhua, Wang Boqun, Yang Shuzhuang, Gu Weijun, Ma Fuxiang, and He Yingqin attended. Chairman Song Ziwen discussed the following matters: (1) The Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry jointly reported that the chambers of commerce in Shanghai and other places, as well as the native cloth industry associations, have successively requested exemption from the business tax on native cloth. Also, since the promulgation of the Business Tax Law, various industries have successively requested reductions and exemptions, some of which are worthy of adoption. The two ministries have repeatedly dispatched personnel to discuss together, and have resolved four principles and measures for reducing and exempting the business tax: 1. All hand-woven fabric industries, where both the supply and demand sides are poor people, should be exempt from the business tax for both the manufacturing and sales industries of handmade native cloth in order to maintain their livelihoods. Stores that also sell other items, but whose main business is selling handmade native cloth, should also have the main part excluded from taxation. 2. Manufacturers or sellers of equipment may be granted a discretionary exemption from the business tax if the central or provincial and municipal governments consider it necessary to promote or maintain them. Those exempted by the provincial and municipal governments should be reported to the Ministry for record. 3. Manufacturers and sellers of necessities of life and other emergency supplies, which have a relief nature under special circumstances such as disasters and famines, may be temporarily exempted from the business tax by the central or provincial and municipal governments in designated areas and periods. Those exempted by the provincial and municipal governments should be reported to the Ministry for record. 4. For domestic indigenous products and handicrafts related to the livelihoods of the poor, if it is necessary to promote and maintain them under special circumstances in international trade, the central or provincial and municipal governments may discretionary reduce or exempt the business tax for their manufacturing or sales industries. Those discretionary reduced or exempted by the provincial and municipal governments should be reported to the Ministry for record. The above measures are proposed to be promulgated to the provincial and municipal governments for compliance. Whether this is appropriate, it is hereby presented for review and implementation. Resolved to proceed as proposed. (2) The Ministry of Navy submitted a revised naval etiquette regulation, requesting review and promulgation. Resolved to approve the revision. (3) The Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the Ministry of Finance, and the Ministry of Education jointly reported that the American People's Art Exhibition has sent a letter requesting our country to participate in the exhibition. The matter was previously submitted to the National Affairs Meeting and resolved to be submitted to the three ministries for review. Having complied with the order, our ministry and others dispatched personnel to consult and review, and all agreed that since the purpose of the meeting is to promote people's art and communicate international culture, it seems necessary for our country to participate. As for the required expenses, it is proposed to temporarily set it at 200,000 national currency. This is hereby jointly presented for review and implementation. Resolved to proceed as proposed. (4) Resolved to approve the request of Zhang Jian'an, a member of the Hebei Provincial Government and Director of the Education Department, to be relieved of his concurrent positions. Zhang Lisheng is to be appointed to succeed him as a member, and Chen Baoquan, the current member, is to be appointed to concurrently serve as Director of the Education Department. (5) Resolved to appoint Liu Xianlin as a lieutenant colonel assistant member of the Ordnance Research Committee of the Ordnance Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs. (6) Resolved to reassign He Yushu, Director of the Agriculture and Mining Department of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, as Director of the Industry Department, and Miao Xijia, Director of the Agriculture and Mining Department of the Yunnan Provincial Government, as Director of the Industry Department. (7) Resolved to approve the request of Liu Fu, Secretary-General of the Anhui Provincial Government, to resign due to another appointment. Wang Huachu is to be appointed to succeed him in the vacant post.

Split in the Guangdong Fourth Plenary Session

The Course of the Dispute Between the Peace Faction and the Power Faction

Guangzhou Correspondence: There were more than 700 representatives at the Fourth Plenary Session of the Guangdong Province. Due to different factions, the situation was quite complicated. There were disputes even before the meeting started. Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, Chen Youren, and others returned to Guangdong from Shanghai with letters from Hu Hanmin, Wang Jingwei, and others. When they discussed the meeting with the local authorities, the Power Faction expressed dissatisfaction with the resolutions of the Seventh Shanghai Peace Conference, especially the item of the first, second, and third Central Committee members serving as natural members of the fourth session. They strongly opposed it and criticized the Guangdong representatives for not implementing the Guomindang's Ma and Ma telegrams, which was extremely harsh. A certain member of the Power Faction, in his report at the commemoration week of the Fourth Plenary Session on the 23rd, stated that the Power Faction's attitude towards personal issues remained unchanged. Later, Sun Ke mediated, explaining the suffering of the Shanghai Peace Conference in seeking compromise, and that it was better to deal with external issues first and not be picky about personal issues. However, the Power Faction still refused to budge. When the Fourth Plenary Session opened, Sun Ke served as chairman. When reading Sun Yat-sen's will, representatives of the Power Faction expressed their anti-Sun attitude at their seats, and some shouted slogans to overthrow Sun Ke. The meeting suddenly became tense. It is said that about 200 of the representatives belonged to the Wang faction, who allied with about 80 to 90 Sun faction representatives to confront the Power Faction representatives. Thus, all the representatives were divided into two factions. The A faction advocated maintaining the resolutions of the Shanghai Peace Conference, while the B faction opposed the resolutions of the Peace Conference. However, the number of representatives in the two factions was greater in the Power Faction, so Sun Ke saw that the situation was not good and advocated suspending the meeting and waiting for Wang Jingwei and Hu Hanmin to return to Guangdong before deliberating. Later, the Power Faction could not wait and, at the second meeting on the 23rd, proposed, in the name of an extraordinary meeting, to reject the resolution of the Shanghai Peace Conference to make the first, second, and third Central Committee members members of the fourth session. The representatives of the Wang and Sun factions opposed it to no avail, and it was eventually passed by a majority vote. Also on that day, Sun Ke knew that the situation was unfavorable and did not attend. The Secretary-General of the Assembly, Li Wenfan, also requested leave on the grounds that he had served as a peace representative in Shanghai. After the victory of the Power Faction, the Wang and Sun factions knew that there was no hope of saving the situation and could not stand in Guangdong. Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, and Chen Youren hurriedly went to Hong Kong on the morning of the 24th. The representatives of the two factions then left Guangdong one after another. The Fourth Plenary Session thus broke down. After Sun and others went to Hong Kong, the Nanhua Newspaper, run by the Wang faction in Hong Kong, fully disclosed the circumstances of the dispute and the pressure they had been subjected to, and made all sorts of disparaging remarks. Zhao Pilian, Guo Chuntao, Bai Yunti, and others among the northern representatives also went to Hong Kong and made statements, expressing their anger at the unreasonableness of the Power Faction. It is estimated that since the 24th, a total of about 200 representatives of the Wang and Sun factions have completely left Guangdong and gone to Hong Kong. Sun Ke, Li Wenfan, and Chen Youren jointly issued a letter to the Fourth Plenary Session of Guangdong, more than a thousand words long, which explained the details of the incident in great detail. Also, after Sun and others left Guangdong, the Fourth Plenary Session was suspended. At the same time, there were many rumors in the market, involving the disintegration of the warlords. However, in fact, no special accidents have occurred in recent days. There was only a slight curfew at night. People in the financial community regarded this turmoil as an opportunity for speculation. Manipulators of central banknotes took the opportunity to act, so the value of central banknotes that had not been cashed in the market fell sharply from the 24th, from 93.4% to 82%. The navy was also slightly on guard during the winter defense period. However, the Fourth Plenary Session still issued a notice on the evening of the 25th, stating that the third formal meeting would continue at 2 pm on the 26th. However, it is still questionable whether there will be a quorum for the meeting after the representatives of the Wang and Sun factions leave. Also, on the evening of the 25th, the Fourth Plenary Session also issued a circular telegram correcting the resolution of the Peace Conference. Its wording was still based on the Ma and Ma telegrams. To sum up, the situation does not seem optimistic. (Evening of November 25th)

Local Correspondence

Suzhou

The Dispute over Donation for Banquets Escalates: The banquet donation in Wuxian County was recently contracted by Han Mutao for 2,300 yuan per month. Han Mutao then entrusted various restaurants to collect the donation from diners on his behalf. Because the restaurants opposed it, a dispute occurred. This donation is designated for educational purposes, so the Bureau of Finance and the Bureau of Education jointly submitted a request to the Provincial Department of Finance and the Provincial Department of Education for instructions. The Provincial Department of Education has issued three proposed measures: (1) Handled by recognized merchants, (2) Revoke the recognized merchants and let the restaurant industry association collect on their behalf, (3) Collected directly by the bureau. The county was ordered to handle the matter carefully. The recognized merchant, Han Mutao, submitted a request to the county government to order the Public Security Bureau to recognize that the representatives of the restaurant industry, Wang Xiangbao and others, were deliberately resisting taxes and asked them to be arrested. Therefore, when the members of the restaurant industry went to the Public Security Bureau to petition on the afternoon of the 30th, the representatives Wang Xiangbao, Zhang Wenbin, Qin Ziyuan, Sun Guichang, and Zhang Xingsheng were detained by the Public Security Bureau. Therefore, the industry held an emergency meeting yesterday (1st) and telegraphed party and government organs and chambers of commerce for assistance. The iron machine, silk weaving, and other 30 industry associations were extremely indignant about this matter. They believed that the restaurant industry was not resisting taxes, but only opposed being the collection agency for the recognized merchant. The Public Security Bureau abused its power and illegally arrested people, which made everyone feel insecure and was undermining commercial operations. They urgently moved to the county chamber of commerce. The county chamber of commerce then convened a meeting at 5 pm yesterday (1st) and immediately resolved to telegraph the provincial government, the provincial department of finance, and the provincial department of education to investigate the matter quickly in order to maintain the rule of law.

Cai Tingkai Came to Suzhou for Inspection: Cai Tingkai, Commander of the Garrison of Beijing and Shanghai, came to Suzhou from Zhenjiang at 3 pm on the 1st to inspect the 60th Division. Division Commander Shen led Zou Battalion Commander of the 3rd Battalion of the 4th Regiment to welcome him at the station. After getting off the train, Cai went to the Division Headquarters on Northeast Street in the city to rest.

Wuxi

Kidnapping and Assault in Xin'an Town: Zou Ruichu, owner of Shuntai East Provisions Store in Xin'an Town, District 13 of the county, is a prominent local figure with considerable land and a thriving business. At 6 PM the night before last, after closing up for the day, Zou Ruichu went to South Street on business. The store's accountant, Hua Qinshun, was at his desk working on the accounts when suddenly five bandits, each armed with a handgun, burst through the door. They fired three shots into the air as a warning and asked where Zou Ruichu was. A shop assistant replied that he was not home. One bandit remained outside to keep watch, while the other four rushed into the inner room, seized Zou's daughter-in-law, Ling Lanfen, and threatened her with a gun. Zou's wife, Mrs. Ma, heard the commotion from upstairs and ran downstairs, forcefully pushing the bandits away. Ling Lanfen managed to escape. The bandits, enraged, fired two shots, wounding Mrs. Ma, and kidnapped Yao Qishi, an apprentice at the store, dragging him outside. As they passed the Xinchang Rice Shop at the end of the street, they also abducted Wang Jian'san, the shop owner, and fled with their captives. Lin Huben, a member of the town's militia, was patrolling the street and, seeing the situation, immediately attempted a rescue. He was shot and wounded by the bandits, who also stole his rifle. As the bandits were boarding a boat with their hostages, the defense corps arrived to surround and capture them. Shots were exchanged, but due to the late hour, the bandits managed to escape with their captives.

Silk Factories Having Received Public Bonds Must Not Suspend Operations Without Reason: After receiving silk industry relief bonds, many silk factories in this county have suspended operations, affecting production. The provincial government, through the Department of Civil Affairs, has instructed the Wuxi County government to strictly order all silk factories that have received public bonds not to suspend operations without reason. Those that have already suspended operations must resume production immediately to provide stability for workers and benefit production.

Train Collision at Wuxi Station: Yesterday morning, after 7 AM, a freight train engine at the Xili Yangqi of Wuxi Railway Station stopped to take on water. A Shanghai-Changzhou down train, the first of the day, arrived from Changzhou. Due to heavy fog, the station failed to switch the tracks properly. As the train entered Yangqi, it collided head-on with the engine. The tracks sustained some damage. Fortunately, there were few passengers, and only a few were injured by the impact. The Wuxi stationmaster quickly arranged for repairs, and traffic has now returned to normal.

Kunshan

Large Gang of Bandits Captured: At Donghe Village, about three miles from the city, seven bandit boats arrived at approximately 7 PM on the 29th. Villagers, seeing the situation, immediately sounded the alarm. Upon hearing the news, the provincial river police stationed at the East Gate immediately sailed to apprehend them. The police force and the chamber of commerce branch also arrived successively, and together they captured all seven bandit boats and twenty-five bandits, male and female, and escorted them to the county government for strict interrogation.

Important News

Xu Zhou Petitioning Student Han Ruchun

Cuts Off Finger to Swear Resistance Against Japan

Writes a Blood Oath Before Sun Yat-Sen's Statue

Nanjing, 1st: The petitioning group of students from the Beiping Republic College paid respects at the mausoleum this morning and will return to Beiping by the Pingpu train this afternoon. The petitioning group of students from Xuzhou paid respects at the mausoleum at 10 AM on the 1st, led by recruitment officers from the Training Department, who guided them through the rituals and administered an oath. A student named Han Ruchun cut off half of the second finger of his left hand with a knife and wrote a blood oath before Sun Yat-Sen's statue, stating, "As long as I live, I vow to resist Japan to the end." He then fainted and was taken back to the Central University for recuperation by the group's medical team. The remaining students returned to school on foot. The group is scheduled to petition the Central Party Headquarters and the National Government on the 2nd.

Establishment of a Visiting Office for Students in the UK

The China Committee of the British Universities China Committee has been established for several years, with the aim of enhancing cultural exchanges between China and the United Kingdom. Vice-chancellors of universities across the UK and individuals from various sectors concerned with Chinese affairs are all members of the committee. Recently, the Chinese and British governments have agreed to allocate £200,000 from the Boxer Indemnity Fund to the committee as a foundation. The interest income, as stipulated by the British Parliament, will primarily be used to achieve the following objectives: (1) inviting Chinese scholars to lecture in the UK and British scholars to lecture in China; (2) assisting Chinese students in the UK in renting suitable accommodation; (3) providing guidance to Chinese students in the UK on academic and related matters; (4) employing Chinese language professors or lecturers to facilitate the teaching of Chinese language and literature in British universities; (5) promoting collaboration between academic luminaries from China and the UK to advance cultural progress. As the committee has not yet received these funds, the aforementioned activities will be implemented somewhat later. However, the committee has already begun collaborating with Mr. Yang Guangzheng, the Chinese Consul-General in London, and the Chinese Students' Union in the UK to provide guidance to Chinese students in the UK. An office has been established at 3 Endsleigh St, London, W.C.I. Chinese students in the UK or those planning to study in the UK who require assistance with admission procedures, renting accommodation, hiring teachers, or internship placement may contact the Honorary Secretary, Mr. H.T. Silcock. Furthermore, the committee is currently collaborating with Consul-General Yang and the Chinese Students' Union in the UK to compile an updated directory of Chinese students in the UK for assessment purposes. It is anticipated that this visiting office will provide significant convenience to Chinese students in the UK.

Middle School Fundraising Held a "Breaking the Piggy Bank" Ceremony Yesterday

Total Donations Exceeded 30,000 Yuan

The Middle School Anti-Japanese Joint Association had previously issued a notice to schools in Shanghai to hold fundraising events for the National Salvation Fund. The deadline was reached a few days ago. Yesterday, a "breaking the piggy bank" ceremony was held at the Municipal Party Headquarters in the afternoon. Representatives from party and government agencies were dispatched to oversee the event. The result was over 30,000 yuan. The details are recorded below:

"Breaking the Piggy Bank" Ceremony: The "breaking the piggy bank" ceremony was held after 1 PM. Yu Zhongbiao from the Municipal Party Headquarters, Wu Bingying from the Public Security Bureau, and Tang Jingxiu from the Municipal Education Bureau were dispatched to oversee the event. Chairman Zhou Jialiang gave a report, briefly stating that the fundraising was divided into two types: one to raise funds to assist Ma Zhanshan, and the other to be used as a National Salvation Fund. Yu Zhongbiao and others then gave speeches, and the "breaking the piggy bank" began. Approximately 30 middle schools participated. After the piggy banks were broken, the yuan, jiao, and copper coins were separated and calculated. The process was not completed until after 8 PM. The total amount was handed over to the Shanghai Bank for safekeeping. In the future, if the funds need to be used, they must be jointly signed by the representatives of the Student Union and the Municipal Party Headquarters.

Approximate Fundraising Amounts: The approximate fundraising amounts are as follows: Minli over 5,000 yuan, Minli Girls' Middle School 2,800 yuan, Youth Middle School over 2,000 yuan, Qingcai 460 yuan, Peiming Girls' Middle School 180 yuan, Huizhong 90 yuan, Tongde Obstetrics 800 yuan, Huiqun Girls' Middle School 320 yuan, Qixiu 90 yuan, Zhaoji 90 yuan, Daxia 216 yuan, Shanghai University 120 yuan, Chinese Women's Physical Education 330 yuan, Zhengfeng 12 yuan, Jingye 712 yuan, Pudong 110 yuan, Tongyi 170 yuan, China Vocational 500 yuan, Cihang Obstetrics 200 yuan.

Weekly Publication: The Anti-Japanese Weekly published by the Propaganda Section of the Middle School Anti-Japanese Association was originally scheduled to be published this Thursday. However, due to the fact that all of the association's staff went to Beijing to petition, the publication was postponed to next Thursday. Students from various schools who wish to submit articles can write to Yuan Jiliang, staff member of Minli Middle School, Dananmen. (New Sound Society)

Fudan Volunteer Army Inspected by Wang Boling

2,000 People Inspected, Results Quite Good

Mr. Wang Gives Detailed Instructions on Military Training

Wang Boling, Director of Youth Volunteer Army Training in Shanghai, returned to Shanghai from Nanjing after the opening of the Fourth Plenary Session. Recognizing the need for proper guidance and understanding of the military training of the Youth Volunteer Army in universities in this city, he especially inspected the student army and volunteer army of Fudan University yesterday morning (December 1st). At approximately 8 AM that day, about 2,000 people, including the school's student army, volunteer army, chemical warfare team, women's rescue team, and the student army of the school's affiliated middle school, had gathered at the school's large parade ground, lined up to await inspection. At approximately 9 AM, Director Wang arrived at the school by car. He then accompanied Lin Jiyong, chairman of the school's military committee, onto the reviewing platform amidst music and began the inspection. First, the military band played music, and inspecting officer Director Wang and others stepped down from the platform to inspect the troops for a week before returning to their original positions. The troops then circled the parade ground once, led by Colonel Zhang Yifei, the general commander of the army, and held a military parade and a march-past to the sound of military music. The special forces of the volunteer army then performed standardized drills, and the chemical warfare team demonstrated smoke screens and bombs. Their techniques were skilled, their steps were neat, and the spirit of the parade was very full. Among them, the school's volunteer team was the best. After the exercises, Director Wang gave a rather long speech, the content of which contained very frank criticisms of the spirit, steps, and various exercises, and sincere contributions and encouragement for the direction of future military training and the efforts to be made in the work. The words were sincere and moved the crowd. The meeting adjourned at approximately 11 AM. It is also heard that the military will hold a large inspection this Saturday and Sunday. In addition to special performances by various teams, the chemical warfare team plans to perform as many as eight or nine types of chemical weapons.
